The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Bulgaria" title="Constitution of Bulgaria">Constitution</a> also provides possibilities of direct democracy, namely petitions and national <a href="/wiki/Referendum" title="Referendum">referenda</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DD-Navi_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DD-Navi-144">[143]</a></sup> Elections are supervised by an independent Central Election Commission that includes members from all major political parties. Parties must register with the commission prior to participating in a national election.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELibrary_of_Congress200617_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELibrary_of_Congress200617-145">[144]</a></sup> Normally, the prime minister-elect is the leader of the party receiving the most votes in parliamentary elections, although this is not always the case.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELibrary_of_Congress200616_111-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELibrary_of_Congress200616-111">[110]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Unlike the prime minister, presidential domestic power is more limited. The directly elected <a href="/wiki/President_of_Bulgaria" title="President of Bulgaria">president</a> serves as <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> and <a href="/wiki/Commander-in-chief" title="Commander-in-chief">commander-in-chief</a> of the armed forces, and has the authority to return a bill for further debate, although the parliament can override the <a href="/wiki/Presidential_veto" class="mw-redirect" title="Presidential veto">presidential veto</a> by a simple majority vote.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELibrary_of_Congress200616_111-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELibrary_of_Congress200616-111">[110]</a></sup> Political parties gather in the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_(Bulgaria)" title="National Assembly (Bulgaria)">National Assembly</a>, a body of 240 deputies elected to four-year terms by direct popular vote. The National Assembly has the power to enact laws, approve the budget, schedule presidential elections, select and dismiss the prime minister and other ministers, declare war, deploy troops abroad, and ratify international treaties and agreements.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELibrary_of_Congress200616–17_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELibrary_of_Congress200616–17-146">[145]</a></sup> </p> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style>
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:249px;max-width:249px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:123px;max-width:123px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Rumen_Radev_official_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="Portrait of president Rumen Radev" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Rumen_Radev_official_%28cropped%29.jpg/121px-Rumen_Radev_official_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="121" height="169" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Rumen_Radev_official_%28cropped%29.jpg/182px-Rumen_Radev_official_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Rumen_Radev_official_%28cropped%29.jpg/242px-Rumen_Radev_official_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="993" data-file-height="1388"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption text-align-center">
           <a href="/wiki/Rumen_Radev" title="Rumen Radev">Rumen Radev</a>
           <br><small><a href="/wiki/President_of_Bulgaria" title="President of Bulgaria">President</a></small>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:122px;max-width:122px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Boyko_Borissov_2017-11-03.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Portrait of premier Boyko Borisov" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Boyko_Borissov_2017-11-03.jpg/120px-Boyko_Borissov_2017-11-03.jpg" decoding="async" width="120" height="169" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Boyko_Borissov_2017-11-03.jpg/180px-Boyko_Borissov_2017-11-03.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Boyko_Borissov_2017-11-03.jpg/240px-Boyko_Borissov_2017-11-03.jpg 2x" data-file-width="511" data-file-height="719"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption text-align-center">
           <a href="/wiki/Boyko_Borisov" title="Boyko Borisov">Boyko Borisov</a>
           <br><small> <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Bulgaria" title="Prime Minister of Bulgaria">Prime Minister</a></small>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Overall, Bulgaria displays a pattern of unstable governments.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[146]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Boyko_Borisov" title="Boyko Borisov">Boyko Borisov</a> is serving his third term as prime minister since 2009,<sup id="cite_ref-WP1_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WP1-148">[147]</a></sup> when his centre-right, pro-EU party <a href="/wiki/GERB" title="GERB">GERB</a> won <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_parliamentary_election,_2009" class="mw-redirect" title="Bulgarian parliamentary election, 2009">the general election</a> and ruled as a <a href="/wiki/Minority_government" title="Minority government">minority government</a> with 117 seats in the National Assembly.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[148]</a></sup> His first government resigned on 20 February 2013 after <a href="/wiki/Protests_against_the_Borisov_cabinet" class="mw-redirect" title="Protests against the Borisov cabinet">nationwide protests</a> caused by high costs of utilities, low living standards, corruption<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[149]</a></sup> and the perceived failure of the democratic system. The protest wave was notable for self-immolations, spontaneous demonstrations and a strong sentiment against political parties.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[150]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The subsequent <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_parliamentary_election,_2013" class="mw-redirect" title="Bulgarian parliamentary election, 2013">snap elections in May</a> resulted in a narrow win for <a href="/wiki/GERB" title="GERB">GERB</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[151]</a></sup> but the <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_Socialist_Party" title="Bulgarian Socialist Party">Bulgarian Socialist Party</a> eventually formed a government led by <a href="/wiki/Plamen_Oresharski" title="Plamen Oresharski">Plamen Oresharski</a> after Borisov failed to secure parliamentary support.<sup id="cite_ref-form_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-form-153">[152]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[153]</a></sup> The Oresharski government resigned in July 2014 amid continuing <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_Bulgarian_protests_against_the_Oresharski_cabinet" class="mw-redirect" title="2013–14 Bulgarian protests against the Oresharski cabinet">large-scale protests</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[154]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[155]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[156]</a></sup> A caretaker government took over<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[157]</a></sup> and called the <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_parliamentary_election,_2014" class="mw-redirect" title="Bulgarian parliamentary election, 2014">October 2014 elections</a><sup id="cite_ref-Sofia_News_Agency_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sofia_News_Agency-159">[158]</a></sup> which resulted in a third GERB victory, but a total of eight parties entered parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[159]</a></sup> Borisov <a href="/wiki/Second_Borisov_Government" title="Second Borisov Government">formed a coalition</a><sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[160]</a></sup> with several right-wing parties, but resigned again after the candidate backed by his party failed to win the <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_presidential_election,_2016" class="mw-redirect" title="Bulgarian presidential election, 2016">2016 Presidential election</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_parliamentary_election,_2017" class="mw-redirect" title="Bulgarian parliamentary election, 2017">March 2017 snap election</a> was again won by GERB, but with 95 seats in Parliament. They formed a coalition with the far-right <a href="/wiki/United_Patriots" title="United Patriots">United Patriots</a>, who hold 27 seats.<sup id="cite_ref-WP1_148-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WP1-148">[147]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Freedom_House" title="Freedom House">Freedom House</a> has reported a continuing deterioration of democratic governance after 2009, citing reduced media independence, stalled reforms, abuse of authority at the highest level and increased dependence of local administrations on the central government.<sup id="cite_ref-FH_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FH-162">[161]</a></sup> Bulgaria is still <a href="/wiki/Freedom_in_the_World" title="Freedom in the World">listed as "Free"</a>, with a political system designated as a semi-consolidated democracy, albeit with deteriorating scores.<sup id="cite_ref-FH_162-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FH-162">[161]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Democracy_Index" title="Democracy Index">Democracy Index</a> defines it as a "Flawed democracy".<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[162]</a></sup> A 2018 survey by the <a href="/wiki/Institute_for_Economics_and_Peace" class="mw-redirect" title="Institute for Economics and Peace">Institute for Economics and Peace</a> reported that less than 15% of respondents considered elections to be fair.<sup id="cite_ref-GPI_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GPI-164">[163]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_system">Legal system</span></h3> 
      <p>Bulgaria has a <a href="/wiki/Civil_law_(legal_system)" title="Civil law (legal system)">civil law</a> legal system.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[164]</a></sup> The judiciary is overseen by the Ministry of Justice. The Supreme Administrative Court and the Supreme Court of Cassation are the highest courts of appeal and oversee the application of laws in subordinate courts.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELibrary_of_Congress200617_145-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELibrary_of_Congress200617-145">[144]</a></sup> The Supreme Judicial Council manages the system and appoints judges. The legal system is regarded by both domestic and international observers as one of Europe's most inefficient due to pervasive lack of transparency and corruption.<sup id="cite_ref-SG1_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SG1-166">[165]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[166]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[167]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[168]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[169]</a></sup> Law enforcement is carried out by organisations mainly subordinate to the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Interior_(Bulgaria)" title="Ministry of Interior (Bulgaria)">Ministry of the Interior</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[170]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/National_Police_Service_(Bulgaria)" title="National Police Service (Bulgaria)">General Directorate of National Police</a> (GDNP) combats general crime and maintains public order.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[171]</a></sup> GDNP fields 26,578 police officers in its local and national sections.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[172]</a></sup> The bulk of criminal cases are transport-related, followed by <a href="/wiki/Theft" title="Theft">theft</a> and drug-related crime; <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_intentional_homicide_rate" title="List of countries by intentional homicide rate">homicide rates are low</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENSI_Brochure201827_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENSI_Brochure201827-174">[173]</a></sup> The Ministry of the Interior also heads the Border Police Service and the <a href="/wiki/Gendarmerie_(Bulgaria)" title="Gendarmerie (Bulgaria)">National Gendarmerie</a>—a specialized branch for anti-terrorist activity, crisis management and riot control. Counterintelligence and national security are the responsibility of the State Agency for National Security.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[174]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Bulgaria" title="Provinces of Bulgaria">Provinces of Bulgaria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Bulgaria" title="Municipalities of Bulgaria">Municipalities of Bulgaria</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Bulgaria is a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary state</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[175]</a></sup> Since the 1880s, the number of territorial management units has varied from seven to 26.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[176]</a></sup> Between 1987 and 1999 the administrative structure consisted of nine provinces (<i>oblasti</i>, singular <i><a href="/wiki/Oblast" title="Oblast">oblast</a></i>). A new administrative structure was adopted in parallel with the decentralization of the economic system.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[177]</a></sup> It includes 27 provinces and a metropolitan capital province (Sofia-Grad). All areas take their names from their respective capital cities. The provinces are subdivided into 265 <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Bulgaria" title="Municipalities of Bulgaria">municipalities</a>. Municipalities are run by mayors, who are elected to four-year terms, and by directly elected municipal councils. Bulgaria is a highly <a href="/wiki/Centralization" class="mw-redirect" title="Centralization">centralized</a> state where the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Bulgaria" title="Government of Bulgaria">Council of Ministers</a> directly appoints regional governors and all provinces and municipalities are heavily dependent on it for funding.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELibrary_of_Congress200617_145-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELibrary_of_Congress200617-145">[144]</a></sup> </p> 
      <table style="margin:auto;" cellpadding="10"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Largest_cities_and_towns">Largest cities and towns</span></h3> 
      <table class="navbox"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th colspan="10" class="navbox-title">

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations_and_security">Foreign relations and security</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Bulgaria" title="Foreign relations of Bulgaria">Foreign relations of Bulgaria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Bulgaria" class="mw-redirect" title="Military of Bulgaria">Military of Bulgaria</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Bulgaria became a member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> in 1955 and since 1966 has been a non-permanent member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">Security Council</a> three times, most recently from 2002 to 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[179]</a></sup> It was also among the founding nations of the <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe</a> (OSCE) in 1975. Euro-Atlantic integration has been a priority since the fall of communism, although the communist leadership also had aspirations of leaving the Warsaw Pact and joining the <a href="/wiki/European_Communities" title="European Communities">European Communities</a> by 1987.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[180]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[181]</a></sup> Bulgaria signed the European Union <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Accession_2005" title="Treaty of Accession 2005">Treaty of Accession</a> on 25 April 2005,<sup id="cite_ref-ec_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ec-183">[182]</a></sup> and became a full member of the European Union on 1 January 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-Ind_114-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ind-114">[113]</a></sup> In addition, it has a tripartite economic and diplomatic collaboration with Romania and Greece,<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[183]</a></sup> good ties with China<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[184]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a><sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[185]</a></sup> and a historical relationship with <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[186]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[187]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[188]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[189]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:BAF_MiG-29s_in_flight_Garchev.png" class="image"><img alt="Bulgarian MiG-29 fighters in flight" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/BAF_MiG-29s_in_flight_Garchev.png/220px-BAF_MiG-29s_in_flight_Garchev.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/BAF_MiG-29s_in_flight_Garchev.png/330px-BAF_MiG-29s_in_flight_Garchev.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/BAF_MiG-29s_in_flight_Garchev.png/440px-BAF_MiG-29s_in_flight_Garchev.png 2x" data-file-width="1149" data-file-height="760"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:BAF_MiG-29s_in_flight_Garchev.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Mikoyan_MiG-29" title="Mikoyan MiG-29">Mikoyan MiG-29</a> jet fighters of the <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_Air_Force" title="Bulgarian Air Force">Bulgarian Air Force</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Bulgaria deployed significant numbers of both civilian and military advisors in Soviet-allied countries like <a href="/wiki/Nicaraguan_Revolution" title="Nicaraguan Revolution">Nicaragua</a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArms_Sales_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArms_Sales-191">[190]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Great_Socialist_People%27s_Libyan_Arab_Jamahiriya" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Socialist People's Libyan Arab Jamahiriya">Libya</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEForeign_Affairs_in_the_1960s_and_1970s_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEForeign_Affairs_in_the_1960s_and_1970s-192">[191]</a></sup> The first deployment of foreign troops on Bulgarian soil since World War II occurred in 2001, when the country hosted six <a href="/wiki/KC-135_Stratotanker" class="mw-redirect" title="KC-135 Stratotanker">KC-135 Stratotanker</a> aircraft and 200 support personnel for the war effort in Afghanistan.<sup id="cite_ref-CENTCOM_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CENTCOM-26">[25]</a></sup> International military relations were further expanded with accession to <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> in March 2004<sup id="cite_ref-nato_113-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nato-113">[112]</a></sup> and the US-Bulgarian Defence Cooperation Agreement signed in April 2006. <a href="/wiki/Bezmer_Air_Base" title="Bezmer Air Base">Bezmer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Graf_Ignatievo_Air_Base" title="Graf Ignatievo Air Base">Graf Ignatievo</a> air bases, the <a href="/wiki/Novo_Selo_Range" title="Novo Selo Range">Novo Selo</a> training range, and a logistics centre in <a href="/wiki/Aytos_Logistics_Center" title="Aytos Logistics Center">Aytos</a> subsequently became <a href="/wiki/List_of_joint_US-Bulgarian_military_bases" class="mw-redirect" title="List of joint US-Bulgarian military bases">joint military training facilities</a> cooperatively used by the United States and Bulgarian militaries.<sup id="cite_ref-State_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-State-193">[192]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[193]</a></sup> Despite its active international defence collaborations, Bulgaria ranks as among the most peaceful countries globally, tying 6th alongside Iceland regarding domestic and international conflicts, and 26th on average in the <a href="/wiki/Global_Peace_Index" title="Global Peace Index">Global Peace Index</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-GPI_164-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GPI-164">[163]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Domestic defence is the responsibility of the all-<a href="/wiki/Volunteer_military" title="Volunteer military">volunteer</a> <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_armed_forces" class="mw-redirect" title="Bulgarian armed forces">Bulgarian armed forces</a>, composed of <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_land_forces" class="mw-redirect" title="Bulgarian land forces">land forces</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_Navy" title="Bulgarian Navy">navy</a> and an <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_Air_Force" title="Bulgarian Air Force">air force</a>. The land forces consist of two mechanized brigades and eight independent regiments and battalions; the air force operates 106 aircraft and air defence systems in six air bases, and the navy operates various ships, helicopters and coastal defence weapons.<sup id="cite_ref-AF_plan_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AF_plan-195">[194]</a></sup> Active troops dwindled from 152,000 in 1988<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMilitary_Personnel_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMilitary_Personnel-196">[195]</a></sup> to 31,300 in 2017, supplemented by 3,000 reservists and 16,000 paramilitary.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[196]</a></sup> Inventory is mostly made up of Soviet equipment like <a href="/wiki/Mikoyan_MiG-29" title="Mikoyan MiG-29">Mikoyan MiG-29</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sukhoi_Su-25" title="Sukhoi Su-25">Sukhoi Su-25</a> jets,<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">[197]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/S-300_missile_system" title="S-300 missile system">S-300PT</a> air defence systems<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[198]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/SS-21_Scarab" class="mw-redirect" title="SS-21 Scarab">SS-21 Scarab</a> short-range <a href="/wiki/Ballistic_missile" title="Ballistic missile">ballistic missiles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">[199]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Bulgaria" title="Economy of Bulgaria">Economy of Bulgaria</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:442px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Economic_Growth_in_Bulgaria.gif" class="image"><img alt="Graph showing GDP and unemployment" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Economic_Growth_in_Bulgaria.gif/440px-Economic_Growth_in_Bulgaria.gif" decoding="async" width="440" height="187" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Economic_Growth_in_Bulgaria.gif/660px-Economic_Growth_in_Bulgaria.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/00/Economic_Growth_in_Bulgaria.gif 2x" data-file-width="870" data-file-height="369"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Economic_Growth_in_Bulgaria.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Economic growth (green) and unemployment (blue) statistics since 2001
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Bulgaria has an open, <a href="/wiki/Developing_country" title="Developing country">upper middle income</a> range <a href="/wiki/Market_economy" title="Market economy">market economy</a> where the private sector accounts for more than 70% of GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">[200]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[201]</a></sup> From a largely agricultural country with a predominantly rural population in 1948, by the 1980s Bulgaria had transformed into an industrial economy with scientific and technological research at the top of its budgetary expenditure priorities.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[202]</a></sup> The loss of <a href="/wiki/COMECON" class="mw-redirect" title="COMECON">COMECON</a> markets in 1990 and the subsequent "<a href="/wiki/Shock_therapy_(economics)" title="Shock therapy (economics)">shock therapy</a>" of the planned system caused a steep decline in industrial and agricultural production, ultimately followed by an economic collapse in 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-Economies_204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Economies-204">[203]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">[204]</a></sup> The economy largely recovered during a period of rapid growth several years later,<sup id="cite_ref-Economies_204-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Economies-204">[203]</a></sup> but the average salary of 1,036 leva ($615) per month remains the lowest in the EU.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">[205]</a></sup> More than a fifth of the labour force are employed on a <a href="/wiki/Minimum_wage" title="Minimum wage">minimum wage</a> of $1.16 per hour.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[206]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A <a href="/wiki/Balanced_budget" title="Balanced budget">balanced budget</a> was achieved in 2003 and the country began running a <a href="/wiki/Budget_surplus" class="mw-redirect" title="Budget surplus">surplus</a> the following year.<sup id="cite_ref-OECD1_208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OECD1-208">[207]</a></sup> Expenditures amounted to $21.15 billion and revenues were $21.67 billion in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">[208]</a></sup> Most government spending on institutions is earmarked for security. The ministries of defence, the interior and justice are allocated the largest share of the annual government budget, whereas those responsible for the environment, tourism and energy receive the least amount of funding.<sup id="cite_ref-2018budget_210-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2018budget-210">[209]</a></sup> Taxes form the bulk of government revenue<sup id="cite_ref-2018budget_210-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2018budget-210">[209]</a></sup> at 30% of GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">[210]</a></sup> Bulgaria has some of the lowest corporate income <a href="/wiki/Tax_rates_in_Europe" title="Tax rates in Europe">tax rates in the EU</a> at a flat 10% rate.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">[211]</a></sup> The tax system is two-tier. <a href="/wiki/Value_added_tax" class="mw-redirect" title="Value added tax">Value added tax</a>, <a href="/wiki/Excise_duties" class="mw-redirect" title="Excise duties">excise duties</a>, corporate and personal income tax are national, whereas real estate, inheritance, and vehicle taxes are levied by local authorities.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">[212]</a></sup> Strong economic performance in the early 2000s reduced <a href="/wiki/Government_debt" title="Government debt">government debt</a> from 79.6% in 1998 to 14.1% in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-OECD1_208-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OECD1-208">[207]</a></sup> It has since increased to 28.7% of GDP by 2016, but remains the third lowest in the EU.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">[213]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Yugozapaden" class="mw-redirect" title="Yugozapaden">Yugozapaden</a> <a href="/wiki/First-level_NUTS_of_the_European_Union" title="First-level NUTS of the European Union">planning area</a> is the most developed region with a <a href="/wiki/Per_capita" title="Per capita">per capita</a> gross domestic product (<a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">PPP</a>) of $29,816 in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">[214]</a></sup> It includes the capital city and the surrounding <a href="/wiki/Sofia_Province" title="Sofia Province">Sofia Province</a>, which alone generate 42% of national gross domestic product despite hosting only 22% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">[215]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENSI_Census_data2017_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENSI_Census_data2017-217">[216]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/GDP" class="mw-redirect" title="GDP">GDP</a> per capita (in PPS) and the cost of living in 2019 stood at 53 and 52.8% of the EU average (100%), respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">[217]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">[218]</a></sup> National PPP GDP was estimated at $143.1&nbsp;billion in 2016, with a per capita value of $20,116.<sup id="cite_ref-imf2_220-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-imf2-220">[219]</a></sup> Economic growth statistics take into account illegal transactions from the <a href="/wiki/Informal_economy" title="Informal economy">informal economy</a>, which is the largest in the EU as a percentage of economic output.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">[220]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">[221]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_National_Bank" title="Bulgarian National Bank">Bulgarian National Bank</a> issues the national currency, <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_lev" title="Bulgarian lev">lev</a>, which is pegged to the euro at a rate of 1.95583 levа per euro.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">[222]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>After several consecutive years of high growth, repercussions of the <a href="/wiki/Financial_crisis_of_2007%E2%80%932008" title="Financial crisis of 2007–2008">financial crisis of 2007–2008</a> resulted in a 3.6% contraction of GDP in 2009 and increased unemployment.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">[223]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">[224]</a></sup> Industrial output declined 10%, mining by 31%, and ferrous and metal production marked a 60% drop.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Positive growth was restored in 2010 but intercompany debt exceeded $59 billion, meaning that 60% of all Bulgarian companies were mutually indebted.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">[225]</a></sup> By 2012, it had increased to $97 billion, or 227% of GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">[226]</a></sup> The government implemented strict austerity measures with IMF and EU encouragement to some positive fiscal results, but the social consequences of these measures, such as increased <a href="/wiki/Economic_inequality" title="Economic inequality">income inequality</a> and accelerated outward migration, have been "catastrophic" according to the <a href="/wiki/International_Trade_Union_Confederation" title="International Trade Union Confederation">International Trade Union Confederation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">[227]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Siphoning of public funds to the families and relatives of politicians from incumbent parties has resulted in fiscal and welfare losses to society.<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">[228]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">[229]</a></sup> Bulgaria ranks 71st in the <a href="/wiki/Corruption_Perceptions_Index" title="Corruption Perceptions Index">Corruption Perceptions Index</a><sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">[230]</a></sup> and experiences the worst levels of <a href="/wiki/Corruption" title="Corruption">corruption</a> in the European Union, a phenomenon that remains a source of profound public discontent.<sup id="cite_ref-cloud_232-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cloud-232">[231]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">[232]</a></sup> Along with organized crime, corruption has resulted in a rejection of the country's <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a> application and withdrawal of foreign investment.<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">[233]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">[234]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-reuters_USKBN1F61EQ_236-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters_USKBN1F61EQ-236">[235]</a></sup> Government officials reportedly engage in embezzlement, influence trading, government procurement violations and bribery with impunity.<sup id="cite_ref-SG1_166-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SG1-166">[165]</a></sup> Government procurement in particular is a critical area in corruption risk. An estimated 10 billion leva ($5.99 billion) of state budget and <a href="/wiki/Structural_Funds_and_Cohesion_Fund" title="Structural Funds and Cohesion Fund">European cohesion</a> funds are spent on public tenders each year;<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">[236]</a></sup> nearly 14 billion ($8.38 billion) were spent on public contracts in 2017 alone.<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">[237]</a></sup> A large share of these contracts are awarded to a few politically connected<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">[238]</a></sup> companies amid widespread irregularities, procedure violations and tailor-made award criteria.<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">[239]</a></sup> Despite repeated criticism from the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-reuters_USKBN1F61EQ_236-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters_USKBN1F61EQ-236">[235]</a></sup> EU institutions refrain from taking measures against Bulgaria because it supports Brussels on a number of issues, unlike <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a> or <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cloud_232-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cloud-232">[231]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Structure_and_sectors">Structure and sectors</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bulgaria_2016_export_treemap.svg" class="image"><img alt="Economic complexity chart showing the various kinds of Bulgarian exports" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Bulgaria_2016_export_treemap.svg/330px-Bulgaria_2016_export_treemap.svg.png" decoding="async" width="330" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Bulgaria_2016_export_treemap.svg/495px-Bulgaria_2016_export_treemap.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Bulgaria_2016_export_treemap.svg/660px-Bulgaria_2016_export_treemap.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1056" data-file-height="463"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bulgaria_2016_export_treemap.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Tree-map of Bulgarian exports in 2016
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The labour force is 3.36&nbsp;million people,<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">[240]</a></sup> of whom 6.8% are employed in agriculture, 26.6% in industry and 66.6% in the services sector.<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">[241]</a></sup> Extraction of metals and minerals, production of <a href="/wiki/Chemical_industry" title="Chemical industry">chemicals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Machinery_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Machinery industry">machine building</a>, steel, biotechnology, tobacco, food processing and <a href="/wiki/Refined_petroleum_fuel" class="mw-redirect" title="Refined petroleum fuel">petroleum refining</a> are among the major industrial activities.<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">[242]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">[243]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">[244]</a></sup> Mining alone employs 24,000 people and generates about 5% of the country's GDP; the number of employed in all mining-related industries is 120,000.<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">[245]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ore_exports_247-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ore_exports-247">[246]</a></sup> Bulgaria is Europe's fifth-largest coal producer.<sup id="cite_ref-Ore_exports_247-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ore_exports-247">[246]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">[247]</a></sup> Local deposits of coal, iron, copper and lead are vital for the manufacturing and energy sectors.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEResource_Base_249-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEResource_Base-249">[248]</a></sup> The main destinations of Bulgarian exports outside the EU are Turkey, China and the United States, while Russia and Turkey are by far the largest import partners. Most of the exports are manufactured goods, machinery, chemicals, fuel products and food.<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">[249]</a></sup> Two-thirds of food and agricultural exports go to <a href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD">OECD</a> countries.<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">[250]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Although cereal and vegetable output dropped by 40% between 1990 and 2008,<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">[251]</a></sup> output in grains has since increased, and the 2016–2017 season registered the biggest grain output in a decade.<sup id="cite_ref-UNdata_253-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNdata-253">[252]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">[253]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">Maize</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barley" title="Barley">barley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oats" class="mw-redirect" title="Oats">oats</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rice" title="Rice">rice</a> are also grown. Quality <a href="/wiki/Turkish_tobacco" title="Turkish tobacco">Oriental tobacco</a> is a significant industrial crop.<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">[254]</a></sup> Bulgaria is also the largest producer globally of <a href="/wiki/Lavender_oil" title="Lavender oil">lavender</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rose_oil" title="Rose oil">rose oil</a>, both widely used in fragrances.<sup id="cite_ref-CENTCOM_26-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CENTCOM-26">[25]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">[255]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">[256]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">[257]</a></sup> Within the services sector, <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Bulgaria" title="Tourism in Bulgaria">tourism</a> is a significant contributor to economic growth. <a href="/wiki/Sofia" title="Sofia">Sofia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plovdiv" title="Plovdiv">Plovdiv</a>, <a href="/wiki/Veliko_Tarnovo" title="Veliko Tarnovo">Veliko Tarnovo</a>, coastal resorts <a href="/wiki/Albena" title="Albena">Albena</a>, <a href="/wiki/Golden_Sands" title="Golden Sands">Golden Sands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sunny_Beach" title="Sunny Beach">Sunny Beach</a> and winter resorts <a href="/wiki/Bansko" title="Bansko">Bansko</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pamporovo" title="Pamporovo">Pamporovo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Borovets" title="Borovets">Borovets</a> are some of the locations most visited by tourists.<sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">[258]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">[259]</a></sup> Most visitors are Romanian, Turkish, Greek and German.<sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">[260]</a></sup> Tourism is additionally encouraged through the <a href="/wiki/100_Tourist_Sites_of_Bulgaria" title="100 Tourist Sites of Bulgaria">100 Tourist Sites</a> system.<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">[261]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Science_and_technology">Science and technology</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Science_and_technology_in_Bulgaria" title="Science and technology in Bulgaria">Science and technology in Bulgaria</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Spending on <a href="/wiki/Research_and_development" title="Research and development">research and development</a> amounts to 0.78% of GDP,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENSI_Brochure201819_263-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENSI_Brochure201819-263">[262]</a></sup> and the bulk of public R&amp;D funding goes to the <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Bulgarian Academy of Sciences">Bulgarian Academy of Sciences</a> (BAS).<sup id="cite_ref-EUpresidency_264-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EUpresidency-264">[263]</a></sup> Private businesses accounted for more than 73% of R&amp;D expenditures and employed 42% of Bulgaria's 22,000 researchers in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-R&amp;D_spending_265-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-R&amp;D_spending-265">[264]</a></sup> The same year, Bulgaria ranked 39th out of 50 countries in the <a href="/wiki/Bloomberg_Innovation_Index" class="mw-redirect" title="Bloomberg Innovation Index">Bloomberg Innovation Index</a>, the highest score being in education (24th) and the lowest in value-added manufacturing (48th).<sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">[265]</a></sup> Chronic government underinvestment in research since 1990 has forced many professionals in science and engineering to leave Bulgaria.<sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">[266]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:BulgariaSat-1_Mission_(35491530485).jpg" class="image"><img alt="A SpaceX Falcon 9 rocket launching BulgariaSat-1 in June 2017" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/BulgariaSat-1_Mission_%2835491530485%29.jpg/170px-BulgariaSat-1_Mission_%2835491530485%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/BulgariaSat-1_Mission_%2835491530485%29.jpg/255px-BulgariaSat-1_Mission_%2835491530485%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/BulgariaSat-1_Mission_%2835491530485%29.jpg/340px-BulgariaSat-1_Mission_%2835491530485%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="3000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:BulgariaSat-1_Mission_(35491530485).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The launch of BulgariaSat-1 by SpaceX
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Despite the lack of funding, research in chemistry, <a href="/wiki/Materials_science" title="Materials science">materials science</a> and <a href="/wiki/Physics" title="Physics">physics</a> remains strong.<sup id="cite_ref-EUpresidency_264-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EUpresidency-264">[263]</a></sup> Antarctic research is actively carried out through the <a href="/wiki/St._Kliment_Ohridski_Base" title="St. Kliment Ohridski Base">St. Kliment Ohridski Base</a> on <a href="/wiki/Livingston_Island" title="Livingston Island">Livingston Island</a> in <a href="/wiki/Western_Antarctica" class="mw-redirect" title="Western Antarctica">Western Antarctica</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">[267]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">[268]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Information_and_communication_technologies" class="mw-redirect" title="Information and communication technologies">information and communication technologies</a> (ICT) sector generates three per cent of economic output and employs 40,000<sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">[269]</a></sup> to 51,000 software engineers.<sup id="cite_ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271">[270]</a></sup> Bulgaria was known as a "Communist <a href="/wiki/Silicon_Valley" title="Silicon Valley">Silicon Valley</a>" during the Soviet era due to its key role in <a href="/wiki/COMECON" class="mw-redirect" title="COMECON">COMECON</a> computing technology production.<sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">[271]</a></sup> The country is a regional leader in <a href="/wiki/Supercomputer" title="Supercomputer">high performance computing</a>: it operates <i>Avitohol</i>, the most powerful supercomputer in Southeast Europe, and will host one of the eight <a href="/wiki/Petascale_computing" title="Petascale computing">petascale</a> <a href="/wiki/European_High-Performance_Computing_Joint_Undertaking" title="European High-Performance Computing Joint Undertaking">EuroHPC</a> supercomputers.<sup id="cite_ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273">[272]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">[273]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Bulgaria has made numerous contributions to <a href="/wiki/Space_exploration" title="Space exploration">space exploration</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Interkosmos_275-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Interkosmos-275">[274]</a></sup> These include two scientific satellites, more than 200 payloads and 300 experiments in Earth orbit, as well as <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_cosmonaut_program" title="Bulgarian cosmonaut program">two cosmonauts</a> since 1971.<sup id="cite_ref-Interkosmos_275-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Interkosmos-275">[274]</a></sup> Bulgaria was the first country to grow <a href="/wiki/Wheat" title="Wheat">wheat</a> and vegetables <a href="/wiki/Plants_in_space" title="Plants in space">in space</a> with its <a href="/wiki/SVET_plant_growth_system" title="SVET plant growth system">Svet</a> <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse" title="Greenhouse">greenhouses</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Mir_space_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Mir space station">Mir space station</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">[275]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277">[276]</a></sup> It was involved in the development of the <a href="/wiki/Granat" title="Granat">Granat</a> <a href="/wiki/Gamma-ray_astronomy" title="Gamma-ray astronomy">gamma-ray observatory</a><sup id="cite_ref-RESS_278-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RESS-278">[277]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Vega_program" title="Vega program">Vega program</a>, particularly in modelling trajectories and guidance <a href="/wiki/Algorithms" class="mw-redirect" title="Algorithms">algorithms</a> for both Vega probes.<sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">[278]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280">[279]</a></sup> Bulgarian instruments have been used in the <a href="/wiki/Exploration_of_Mars" title="Exploration of Mars">exploration of Mars</a>, including a spectrometer that took the first high quality <a href="/wiki/Spectroscopy" title="Spectroscopy">spectroscopic</a> images of Martian moon <a href="/wiki/Phobos_(moon)" title="Phobos (moon)">Phobos</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Phobos_2" title="Phobos 2">Phobos 2</a> probe.<sup id="cite_ref-Interkosmos_275-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Interkosmos-275">[274]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RESS_278-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RESS-278">[277]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cosmic_ray" title="Cosmic ray">Cosmic radiation</a> en route to and around the planet has been mapped by <a href="/wiki/Liulin_type_instruments" title="Liulin type instruments">Liulin-ML</a> dosimeters on the <a href="/wiki/ExoMars_Trace_Gas_Orbiter" class="mw-redirect" title="ExoMars Trace Gas Orbiter">ExoMars TGO</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281">[280]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/RADOM-7" title="RADOM-7">Variants</a> of these instruments have also been fitted on the <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">International Space Station</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Chandrayaan-1" title="Chandrayaan-1">Chandrayaan-1</a> lunar probe.<sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282">[281]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-283" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-283">[282]</a></sup> Another lunar mission, <a href="/wiki/SpaceIL" title="SpaceIL">SpaceIL</a>'s <i>Beresheet</i>, was also equipped with a Bulgarian-manufactured imaging payload.<sup id="cite_ref-284" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-284">[283]</a></sup> Bulgaria's first <a href="/wiki/Geosynchronous_satellite" title="Geosynchronous satellite">geostationary communications satellite</a>—<a href="/wiki/BulgariaSat-1" title="BulgariaSat-1">BulgariaSat-1</a>—was launched by <a href="/wiki/SpaceX" title="SpaceX">SpaceX</a> in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285">[284]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_Bulgaria" title="Energy in Bulgaria">Energy in Bulgaria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Bulgaria" title="Transport in Bulgaria">Transport in Bulgaria</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Trakiya_highway_04.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Trakiya motorway, one of the main national motorways" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Trakiya_highway_04.jpg/220px-Trakiya_highway_04.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Trakiya_highway_04.jpg/330px-Trakiya_highway_04.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Trakiya_highway_04.jpg/440px-Trakiya_highway_04.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Trakiya_highway_04.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Trakia_motorway" title="Trakia motorway">Trakia motorway</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Telephone services are widely available, and a central digital trunk line connects most regions.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELibrary_of_Congress200614_286-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELibrary_of_Congress200614-286">[285]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Vivacom" title="Vivacom">Vivacom</a> (BTC) serves more than 90% of fixed lines and is one of the three operators providing mobile services, along with <a href="/wiki/Mtel_(Bulgaria)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mtel (Bulgaria)">A1</a> and <a href="/wiki/Telenor_(Bulgaria)" title="Telenor (Bulgaria)">Telenor</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287">[286]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-288" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-288">[287]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Internet" title="Internet">Internet</a> penetration stood at 66.8% of the population aged 16–74 and 75.1% of households, in 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-289" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-289">[288]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-290" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-290">[289]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Bulgaria's strategic geographic location and well-developed energy sector make it a key European energy centre despite its lack of significant fossil fuel deposits.<sup id="cite_ref-291" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-291">[290]</a></sup> Thermal power plants generate 48.9% of electricity, followed by <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power" title="Nuclear power">nuclear power</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Kozloduy_Nuclear_Power_Plant" title="Kozloduy Nuclear Power Plant">Kozloduy reactors</a> (34.8%) and <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">renewable sources</a> (16.3%).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENSI_Brochure201847_292-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENSI_Brochure201847-292">[291]</a></sup> Equipment for a second nuclear power station at <a href="/wiki/Belene_Nuclear_Power_Plant" title="Belene Nuclear Power Plant">Belene</a> has been acquired, but the fate of the project remains uncertain.<sup id="cite_ref-293" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-293">[292]</a></sup> Installed capacity amounts to 12,668 MW, allowing Bulgaria to exceed domestic demand and export energy.<sup id="cite_ref-294" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-294">[293]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The national road network has a total length of 19,512 kilometres (12,124&nbsp;mi),<sup id="cite_ref-295" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-295">[294]</a></sup> of which 19,235 kilometres (11,952&nbsp;mi) are paved. Railroads are a major mode of freight transportation, although highways carry a progressively larger share of freight. Bulgaria has 6,238 kilometres (3,876&nbsp;mi) of railway track<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELibrary_of_Congress200614_286-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELibrary_of_Congress200614-286">[285]</a></sup> and currently a total of 81 kilometres (50 miles) of <a href="/wiki/High-speed_rail" title="High-speed rail">high-speed lines</a> are in operation.<sup id="cite_ref-296" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-296">[295]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-297" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-297">[296]</a></sup> Rail links are available with Romania, Turkey, Greece, and Serbia, and express trains serve direct routes to <a href="/wiki/Kyiv" title="Kyiv">Kyiv</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minsk" title="Minsk">Minsk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg" title="Saint Petersburg">Saint Petersburg</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-298" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-298">[297]</a></sup> Sofia and Plovdiv are the country's air travel hubs, while Varna and Burgas are the principal maritime trade ports.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELibrary_of_Congress200614_286-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELibrary_of_Congress200614-286">[285]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Bulgaria" title="Demographics of Bulgaria">Demographics of Bulgaria</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bulgaria-demography.png" class="image"><img alt="Population graph" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Bulgaria-demography.png/220px-Bulgaria-demography.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Bulgaria-demography.png/330px-Bulgaria-demography.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Bulgaria-demography.png/440px-Bulgaria-demography.png 2x" data-file-width="785" data-file-height="470"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bulgaria-demography.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Population trend since 1960
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bulgariapop.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Bulgariapop.svg/220px-Bulgariapop.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Bulgariapop.svg/330px-Bulgariapop.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Bulgariapop.svg/440px-Bulgariapop.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bulgariapop.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Population_pyramid" title="Population pyramid">Population pyramid</a> of Bulgaria in 2017
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The population of Bulgaria is 7,364,570 people according to the 2011 national census. The majority of the population, 72.5%, reside in urban areas.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENSI_Census_data20113_299-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENSI_Census_data20113-299">[298]</a></sup> As of 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bulgaria&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Sofia is the most populated urban centre with 1,241,675 people, followed by <a href="/wiki/Plovdiv" title="Plovdiv">Plovdiv</a> (346,893), <a href="/wiki/Varna" title="Varna">Varna</a> (336,505), <a href="/wiki/Burgas" title="Burgas">Burgas</a> (202,434) and <a href="/wiki/Ruse,_Bulgaria" title="Ruse, Bulgaria">Ruse</a> (142,902).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENSI_Census_data2017_217-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENSI_Census_data2017-217">[216]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bulgarians" title="Bulgarians">Bulgarians</a> are the main ethnic group and constitute 84.8% of the population. <a href="/wiki/Turks_in_Bulgaria" class="mw-redirect" title="Turks in Bulgaria">Turkish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roma_in_Bulgaria" class="mw-redirect" title="Roma in Bulgaria">Roma</a> minorities account for 8.8 and 4.9%, respectively; some 40 smaller minorities account for 0.7%, and 0.8% do not self-identify with an ethnic group.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENSI_Census_data20114_300-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENSI_Census_data20114-300">[299]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NSI3_301-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NSI3-301">[300]</a></sup> Former <a href="/wiki/National_Statistical_Institute_(Bulgaria)" title="National Statistical Institute (Bulgaria)">Statistics</a> head <a href="/wiki/Reneta_Indzhova" title="Reneta Indzhova">Reneta Indzhova</a> has disputed the 2011 census figures, suggesting the actual population is smaller than reported.<sup id="cite_ref-302" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-302">[301]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-303" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-303">[302]</a></sup> The Roma minority is usually underestimated in census data and may represent up to 11% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-304" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-304">[303]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-305" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-305">[304]</a></sup> Population density is 65 per square kilometre, almost half the European Union average.<sup id="cite_ref-306" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-306">[305]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2018 the average <a href="/wiki/Total_fertility_rate" title="Total fertility rate">total fertility rate</a> (TFR) across Bulgaria was 1.56 children per woman,<sup id="cite_ref-307" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-307">[306]</a></sup> below the replacement rate of 2.1, it remains considerably below the high of 5.83 children per woman in 1905.<sup id="cite_ref-308" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-308">[307]</a></sup> Bulgaria subsequently has one of the oldest populations in the world, with the average age of 43 years.<sup id="cite_ref-309" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-309">[308]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Bulgaria is in a state of demographic crisis.<sup id="cite_ref-310" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-310">[309]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BNR_crisis_311-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BNR_crisis-311">[310]</a></sup> It has had negative population growth since the early 1990s, when the economic collapse caused a long-lasting emigration wave.<sup id="cite_ref-DW_Entry_312-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DW_Entry-312">[311]</a></sup> Some 937,000 to 1,200,000 people—mostly young adults—left the country by 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-DW_Entry_312-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DW_Entry-312">[311]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-313" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-313">[312]</a></sup> The majority of children are born to unmarried women.<sup id="cite_ref-314" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-314">[313]</a></sup> Furthermore, a third of all households consist of only one person and 75.5% of families do not have children under the age of 16.<sup id="cite_ref-BNR_crisis_311-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BNR_crisis-311">[310]</a></sup> The resulting birth rates are among the lowest in the world<sup id="cite_ref-315" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-315">[314]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-316" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-316">[315]</a></sup> while <a href="/wiki/Death_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Death rate">death rates</a> are among the highest.<sup id="cite_ref-317" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-317">[316]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>High death rates result from a combination of an ageing population, a high number of people at risk of poverty and a weak healthcare system.<sup id="cite_ref-318" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-318">[317]</a></sup> More than 80% of all deaths are due to <a href="/wiki/Cancer" title="Cancer">cancer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cardiovascular_conditions" class="mw-redirect" title="Cardiovascular conditions">cardiovascular conditions</a>; nearly a fifth of those are avoidable.<sup id="cite_ref-319" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-319">[318]</a></sup> Mortality rates can be sharply reduced to levels below the EU average through timely and adequate access to medical services, which the healthcare system does not provide fully.<sup id="cite_ref-320" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-320">[319]</a></sup> Although <a href="/wiki/Healthcare_in_Bulgaria" class="mw-redirect" title="Healthcare in Bulgaria">healthcare in Bulgaria</a> is nominally universal,<sup id="cite_ref-Health_system_321-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Health_system-321">[320]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Out-of-pocket_expenses" class="mw-redirect" title="Out-of-pocket expenses">out-of-pocket expenses</a> account for nearly half of all healthcare spending, which significantly limits access to medical care.<sup id="cite_ref-322" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-322">[321]</a></sup> Other problems disrupting care provision are the emigration of doctors due to low wages, understaffed and under-equipped regional hospitals, supply shortages and frequent changes to the basic service package for those insured.<sup id="cite_ref-323" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-323">[322]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-324" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-324">[323]</a></sup> The 2018 Bloomberg Health Care Efficiency Index ranked Bulgaria last out of 56 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-325" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-325">[324]</a></sup> Average <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">life expectancy</a> is 74.8 years compared with an EU average of 80.99 and a world average of 72.38.<sup id="cite_ref-326" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-326">[325]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-327" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-327">[326]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Sofia_University_%22St._Kliment_Ohridski%22_(37849719131).jpg" class="image"><img alt="Sofia University building" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Sofia_University_%22St._Kliment_Ohridski%22_%2837849719131%29.jpg/220px-Sofia_University_%22St._Kliment_Ohridski%22_%2837849719131%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="178" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Sofia_University_%22St._Kliment_Ohridski%22_%2837849719131%29.jpg/330px-Sofia_University_%22St._Kliment_Ohridski%22_%2837849719131%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Sofia_University_%22St._Kliment_Ohridski%22_%2837849719131%29.jpg/440px-Sofia_University_%22St._Kliment_Ohridski%22_%2837849719131%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3712" data-file-height="3006"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Sofia_University_%22St._Kliment_Ohridski%22_(37849719131).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The Rectorate of Sofia University
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>Public expenditures for education are far below the European Union average as well.<sup id="cite_ref-UNICEF_328-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNICEF-328">[327]</a></sup> Educational standards <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Bulgaria" title="Education in Bulgaria">were once high</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELibrary_of_Congress20066_329-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELibrary_of_Congress20066-329">[328]</a></sup> but have declined significantly since the early 2000s.<sup id="cite_ref-UNICEF_328-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNICEF-328">[327]</a></sup> Bulgarian students were among the highest-scoring in the world in terms of reading in 2001, performing better than their Canadian and German counterparts; by 2006, scores in reading, math and science had dropped. By 2018, <a href="/wiki/Programme_for_International_Student_Assessment" title="Programme for International Student Assessment">Programme for International Student Assessment</a> studies found 47% of pupils in the 9th grade to be <a href="/wiki/Functional_illiteracy" title="Functional illiteracy">functionally illiterate</a> in reading and natural sciences.<sup id="cite_ref-330" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-330">[329]</a></sup> Average basic <a href="/wiki/Literacy" title="Literacy">literacy</a> stands high at 98.4% with no significant difference between sexes.<sup id="cite_ref-331" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-331">[330]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Education_and_Science_(Bulgaria)" title="Ministry of Education and Science (Bulgaria)">Ministry of Education and Science</a> partially funds public schools, colleges and universities, sets criteria for textbooks and oversees the publishing process. Education in primary and secondary public schools is free and compulsory.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELibrary_of_Congress20066_329-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELibrary_of_Congress20066-329">[328]</a></sup> The process spans through 12 grades, where grades one through eight are primary and nine through twelve are secondary level. Higher education consists of a 4-year <a href="/wiki/Bachelor%27s_degree" title="Bachelor's degree">bachelor</a> degree and a 1-year master's degree.<sup id="cite_ref-332" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-332">[331]</a></sup> Bulgaria's highest-ranked higher education institution is <a href="/wiki/Sofia_University" title="Sofia University">Sofia University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-333" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-333">[332]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-334" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-334">[333]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_language" title="Bulgarian language">Bulgarian</a> is the only language with official status and native for 85% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-335" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-335">[334]</a></sup> It belongs to the <a href="/wiki/Slavic_group_of_languages" class="mw-redirect" title="Slavic group of languages">Slavic group of languages</a>, but it has a number of grammatical peculiarities, shared with its closest relative <a href="/wiki/Macedonian_language" title="Macedonian language">Macedonian</a>, that set it apart from other Slavic languages: these include a complex verbal morphology (which also codes for distinctions in <a href="/wiki/Evidentiality" title="Evidentiality">evidentiality</a>), the absence of <a href="/wiki/Noun_cases" class="mw-redirect" title="Noun cases">noun cases</a> and <a href="/wiki/Infinitives" class="mw-redirect" title="Infinitives">infinitives</a>, and the use of a suffixed <a href="/wiki/Definite_article" class="mw-redirect" title="Definite article">definite article</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-336" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-336">[335]</a></sup> Other major languages are <a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Romani_language" title="Romani language">Romani</a>, which according to the 2011 census were spoken natively by 9.1% and 4.2% respectively. </p>
      <p>The country scores high in <a href="/wiki/Gender_equality" title="Gender equality">gender equality</a>, ranking 18th in the 2018 <a href="/wiki/Global_Gender_Gap_Report" title="Global Gender Gap Report">Global Gender Gap Report</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-WEF_337-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WEF-337">[336]</a></sup> Although <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_suffrage" title="Women's suffrage">women's suffrage</a> was enabled relatively late, in 1937, women today have equal political rights, high workforce participation and legally mandated <a href="/wiki/Equal_pay_for_equal_work" title="Equal pay for equal work">equal pay</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-WEF_337-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WEF-337">[336]</a></sup> Bulgaria has the highest ratio of female ICT researchers in the EU,<sup id="cite_ref-338" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-338">[337]</a></sup> as well as the second-highest ratio of females in the technology sector at 44.6% of the workforce. High levels of female participation are a legacy of the Socialist era.<sup id="cite_ref-339" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-339">[338]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Bulgaria" title="Religion in Bulgaria">Religion in Bulgaria</a>
      </div> 
      <p>More than three-quarters of Bulgarians subscribe to <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodoxy" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Orthodoxy">Eastern Orthodoxy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENSI_Census_data20115_340-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENSI_Census_data20115-340">[339]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Muslims" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunni Muslims">Sunni Muslims</a> are the second-largest religious community and constitute 10% of Bulgaria's overall religious makeup, although a majority of them are not observant and find the use of <a href="/wiki/Islamic_veil" class="mw-redirect" title="Islamic veil">Islamic veils</a> in schools unacceptable.<sup id="cite_ref-341" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-341">[340]</a></sup> Less than 3% of the population are affiliated with <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Bulgaria" title="Religion in Bulgaria">other religions</a> and 11.8% are irreligious or do not self-identify with a religion.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENSI_Census_data20115_340-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENSI_Census_data20115-340">[339]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_Orthodox_Church" title="Bulgarian Orthodox Church">Bulgarian Orthodox Church</a> gained <a href="/wiki/Autocephalous" class="mw-redirect" title="Autocephalous">autocephalous</a> status in AD 927,<sup id="cite_ref-342" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-342">[341]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-343" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-343">[342]</a></sup> and has 12 dioceses and over 2,000 priests.<sup id="cite_ref-344" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-344">[343]</a></sup> Bulgaria is a <a href="/wiki/Secular_state" title="Secular state">secular state</a> with guaranteed religious freedom by constitution, but Orthodoxy is designated as a "traditional" religion.<sup id="cite_ref-345" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-345">[344]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Bulgaria" title="Culture of Bulgaria">Culture of Bulgaria</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kukeri_E8.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Bulgarian Kuker" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Kukeri_E8.jpg/220px-Kukeri_E8.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="196" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Kukeri_E8.jpg/330px-Kukeri_E8.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Kukeri_E8.jpg/440px-Kukeri_E8.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3057" data-file-height="2720"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kukeri_E8.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><i>Kuker</i> in <a href="/wiki/Lesichovo" title="Lesichovo">Lesichovo</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Contemporary Bulgarian culture blends the formal culture that helped forge a national consciousness towards the end of Ottoman rule with millennia-old folk traditions.<sup id="cite_ref-Cultural_life_346-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cultural_life-346">[345]</a></sup> An essential element of Bulgarian folklore is fire, used to banish evil spirits and illnesses. Many of these are personified as witches, whereas other creatures like <a href="/wiki/Slavic_dragon" title="Slavic dragon">zmey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Samodiva_(mythology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Samodiva (mythology)">samodiva</a> (<a href="/wiki/Supernatural_beings_in_Slavic_folklore" class="mw-redirect" title="Supernatural beings in Slavic folklore">veela</a>) are either benevolent guardians or ambivalent tricksters.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMacDermott199864–70_347-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacDermott199864–70-347">[346]</a></sup> Some rituals against evil spirits have survived and are still practised, most notably <a href="/wiki/Kukeri" title="Kukeri">kukeri</a> and <a href="/wiki/Survakane" title="Survakane">survakari</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-348" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-348">[347]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Martenitsa" title="Martenitsa">Martenitsa</a> is also widely celebrated.<sup id="cite_ref-349" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-349">[348]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nestinarstvo" class="mw-redirect" title="Nestinarstvo">Nestinarstvo</a>, a ritual fire-dance of Thracian origin, is included in the list of <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_Intangible_Cultural_Heritage_Lists" title="UNESCO Intangible Cultural Heritage Lists">UNESCO Intangible Cultural Heritage</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMacDermott1998226_350-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacDermott1998226-350">[349]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-351" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-351">[350]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/List_of_World_Heritage_Sites_in_Bulgaria" title="List of World Heritage Sites in Bulgaria">Nine historical and natural objects</a> are <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_Site" class="mw-redirect" title="UNESCO World Heritage Site">UNESCO World Heritage Sites</a>: <a href="/wiki/Pirin_National_Park" title="Pirin National Park">Pirin National Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Srebarna_Nature_Reserve" title="Srebarna Nature Reserve">Sreburna Nature Reserve</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Madara_Rider" title="Madara Rider">Madara Rider</a>, the Thracian tombs in <a href="/wiki/Thracian_Tomb_of_Sveshtari" title="Thracian Tomb of Sveshtari">Sveshtari</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thracian_Tomb_of_Kazanlak" title="Thracian Tomb of Kazanlak">Kazanlak</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Rila_Monastery" title="Rila Monastery">Rila Monastery</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Boyana_Church" title="Boyana Church">Boyana Church</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Rock-hewn_Churches_of_Ivanovo" title="Rock-hewn Churches of Ivanovo">Rock-hewn Churches of Ivanovo</a> and the ancient city of <a href="/wiki/Nesebar" title="Nesebar">Nesebar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-352" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-352">[351]</a></sup> The Rila Monastery was established by Saint <a href="/wiki/John_of_Rila" title="John of Rila">John of Rila</a>, Bulgaria's <a href="/wiki/Patron_saint" title="Patron saint">patron saint</a>, whose life has been the subject of numerous literary accounts since Medieval times.<sup id="cite_ref-EBLiterature_353-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EBLiterature-353">[352]</a></sup> </p>
